City of Martinsburg\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Martinsburg\n       </b>\n       is a city in and the\n       <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">\n        county seat\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_County,_West_Virginia" title="Berkeley County, West Virginia">\n        Berkeley County, West Virginia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR6_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GR6-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in the tip of the state\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Panhandle_of_West_Virginia" title="Eastern Panhandle of West Virginia">\n        Eastern Panhandle\n       </a>\n       region. Its population was 17,687 in the 2016 census, making it the largest city in the Eastern Panhandle and the ninth-largest municipality in the state. Martinsburg is part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hagerstown_Metropolitan_Area" title="Hagerstown Metropolitan Area">\n        Hagerstown-Martinsburg, MD-WV Metropolitan Statistical Area\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4">\n         <a href="#Demographics">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n href="#2010_census">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             2010 census\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6">\n           <a href="#2000_census">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             2000 census\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7">\n           <a href="#Climate">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             3.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Climate\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8">\n         <a href="#Commerce">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Commerce\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9">\n         <a href="#Sports">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Sports\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">\n         <a href="#Healthcare">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Healthcare\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11">\n         <a href="#Shopping">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Shopping\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12">\n         <a href="#Education">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Education\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Elementary_.26_Intermediate_Schools">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Elementary &amp; Intermediate Schools\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n           <a href="#Middle_Schools">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Middle Schools\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#High_Schools">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             High Schools\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a href="#Colleges_and_universities">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Colleges and universities\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17">\n         <a href="#Transportation">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Transportation\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18">\n           <a href="#Major_highways">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Major highways\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a href="#Mass_transportation">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Mass transportation\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20">\n         <a href="#Media">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Media\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21">\n           <a href="#Print">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Print\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22">\n           <a href="#Radio">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Radio\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23">\n           <a href="#Television">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Television\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24">\n         <a href="#Notable_people">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Notable people\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Martinsburg was established by an act\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       of the Virginia General Assembly that was adopted in December 1778\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       during the American Revolutionary War. Founder Major General\n       <a href="/wiki/Adam_Stephen" title="Adam Stephen">\n        Adam Stephen\n       </a>\n       named the gateway town to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shenandoah_Valley" title="Shenandoah Valley">\n        Shenandoah Valley\n       </a>\n       along\n       <a href="/wiki/Tuscarora_Creek_(Opequon_Creek)" title="Tuscarora Creek (Opequon Creek)">\n        Tuscarora Creek\n       </a>\n       in honor of Colonel\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bryan_Martin" title="Thomas Bryan Martin">\n        Thomas Bryan Martin\n       </a>\n       , a nephew of\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Fairfax,_6th_Lord_Fairfax_of_Cameron" title="Thomas Fairfax, 6th Lord Fairfax of Cameron">\n        Thomas Fairfax, 6th Lord Fairfax of Cameron\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Aspen_Hall_(Martinsburg,_West_Virginia)" title="Aspen Hall (Martinsburg, West Virginia)">\n        Aspen Hall\n       </a>\n       is a Georgian mansion, the oldest house in the city. Part was built in 1745 by Edward Beeson, Sr. Aspen Hall and its wealthy residents had key roles in the agricultural, religious, transportation, and political history of the region. Significant events related to the\n       <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">\n        French and Indian War\n       </a>\n       ; the Revolution, and the Civil War took place on the property. Three original buildings are still standing, including the rare blockhouse of Mendenhall\'s Fort.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first United States post office in what is now West Virginia was established at Martinsburg in 1792. At that time, Martinsburg and the larger territory were still part of Virginia.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_and_Ohio_employees_magazine_(1912)_(14575208137).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2350" data-file-width="3788" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Baltimore_and_Ohio_employees_magazine_%281912%29_%2814575208137%29.jpg/275px-Baltimore_and_Ohio_employees_magazine_%281912%29_%2814575208137%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Baltimore_and_Ohio_employees_magazine_%281912%29_%2814575208137%29.jpg/413px-Baltimore_and_Ohio_employees_magazine_%281912%29_%2814575208137%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Baltimore_and_Ohio_employees_magazine_%281912%29_%2814575208137%29.jpg/550px-Baltimore_and_Ohio_employees_magazine_%281912%29_%2814575208137%29.jpg 2x" width="275"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baltimore_and_Ohio_employees_magazine_(1912)_(14575208137).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The Baltimore and Ohio\'s Martinsburg Shops three years before the Civil War\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_and_Ohio_Railroad" title="Baltimore and Ohio Railroad">\n        Baltimore and Ohio Railroad\n       </a>\n       (B&amp;O) reached Martinsburg in 1842. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_and_Ohio_Railroad_Martinsburg_Shops" title="Baltimore and Ohio Railroad Martinsburg Shops">\n        Baltimore and Ohio Railroad Martinsburg Shops\n       </a>\n       were constructed in 1849 and rebuilt after the American Civil War.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:3_B%26O_Freight_Train_Photos_at_Martinsburg,_W._VA._(27437398010).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1462" data-file-width="2000" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/3_B%26O_Freight_Train_Photos_at_Martinsburg%2C_W._VA._%2827437398010%29.jpg/220px-3_B%26O_Freight_Train_Photos_at_Martinsburg%2C_W._VA._%2827437398010%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/3_B%26O_Freight_Train_Photos_at_Martinsburg%2C_W._VA._%2827437398010%29.jpg/330px-3_B%26O_Freight_Train_Photos_at_Martinsburg%2C_W._VA._%2827437398010%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/3_B%26O_Freight_Train_Photos_at_Martinsburg%2C_W._VA._%2827437398010%29.jpg/440px-3_B%26O_Freight_Train_Photos_at_Martinsburg%2C_W._VA._%2827437398010%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:3_B%26O_Freight_Train_Photos_at_Martinsburg,_W._VA._(27437398010).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         An engineer waves from a passing B&amp;O freight train in 1969. The B&amp;O\'s shops employed many locals throughout its 130 years of operation.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       According to\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Still" title="William Still">\n        William Still\n       </a>\n       , "The Father of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Underground_Railroad" title="Underground Railroad">\n        Underground Railroad\n       </a>\n       " and its historian, Robert Brown, alias Thomas Jones, escaped from slavery in Martinsburg on Christmas night, 1856. He rode a horse and had it swim across the freezing Potomac River. After riding forty miles, he walked in cold wet clothes for two days, to\n       <a href="/wiki/Harrisburg,_Pennsylvania" title="Harrisburg, Pennsylvania">\n        Harrisburg, Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       . He received assistance there from the Underground Railroad and traveled by train to\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">\n        Philadelphia\n       </a>\n       , and the office of William Still with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania_Anti-Slavery_Society" title="Pennsylvania Anti-Slavery Society">\n        Pennsylvania Anti-Slavery Society\n       </a>\n       . Brown\'s wife and four children had been sold; he sought help to find them. He had a likeness of his wife, and locks of hair from each of them.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2015)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1854, ten-year-old\n       <a href="/wiki/Belle_Boyd" title="Belle Boyd">\n        Isabelle Boyd\n       </a>\n       , known as "Belle" and later a noted spy for the Confederacy, moved to Martinsburg with her family; where her father Benjamin operated a general merchandise store. After the Civil War began, Benjamin joined the Second Virginia Infantry, which was part of the Stonewall Brigade. His wife Mary was thus in charge of the Boyd home when Union forces under General\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Patterson" title="Robert Patterson">\n        Robert Patterson\n       </a>\n       took Martinsburg. When a group of Patterson\'s men tried to raise a Union flag over the Boyd home, Mary refused. One of the soldiers, Frederick Martin, threatened Mary, and Belle shot him. She was acquitted.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       She soon became involved in espionage, sending information to Confederate generals\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_%22Stonewall%22_Jackson" title=\'Thomas "Stonewall" Jackson\'>\n        Thomas "Stonewall" Jackson\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J.E.B._Stuart" title="J.E.B. Stuart">\n        J.E.B. "Jeb" Stuart\n       </a>\n       . Often she was helped by Eliza Corsey, a Boyd family slave whom Belle had taught to read and write. In 1863, Belle was arrested in Martinsburg by the Union Army and imprisoned. Boyd\'s Greek Revival home, which he had built in 1853 and sold in 1855, had numerous owners over the decades. In 1992 it was purchased by the\n       <a class="external text" href="http://www.bchs.org/" rel="nofollow">\n        Berkeley County Historical Society\n       </a>\n       . The historical society renovated the building and now operates it as the Berkeley County Museum. It is also known as the Belle Boyd House.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Most residents of West Virginia were yeomen farmers who supported the Union and, during the Civil War, they voted to separate from Virginia. The new state was admitted to the Union during the war. The city of Martinsburg was incorporated by an act of the new\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Legislature" title="West Virginia Legislature">\n        West Virginia Legislature\n       </a>\n       on March 30, 1868.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Martinsburg became a center of the railroad industry and its workers. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Railroad_Strike_of_1877" title="Great Railroad Strike of 1877">\n        Great Railroad Strike of 1877\n       </a>\n       began July 14, 1877 in this city at the B&amp;O shops\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and spread nationwide.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Telephone service was established in Martinsburg in 1883. In 1889, electricity began to be furnished to Martinsburg as part of a franchise granted to the United Edison Manufacturing Company of New York.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="external text" href="https://www.wvencyclopedia.org/articles/863" rel="nofollow">\n        Interwoven mills\n       </a>\n       began operations in Martinsburg in 1891; it grew to be the largest manufacturer of men\'s hosiery in the world.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Construction of the "Apollo Civic Theatre" was completed in 1913.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Over one thousand (1,039) men from Berkeley County participated in World War I. Of these, forty-one were killed and twenty-one were wounded in battle. A monument to those who fell in battle was erected in Martinsburg in 1925.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During World War II, the Newton D. Baker Hospital in Martinsburg treated thousands of soldiers wounded in the war. In 1946 this military hospital became a part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veterans_Administration" title="Veterans Administration">\n        Veterans Administration\n       </a>\n       (VA). The VA Medical Center in Martinsburg still provides care to United States veterans.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Due to restructuring beginning in the late 1940s and continuing through the 1970s, many of the mills and factories operating in Martinsburg shut down and went out of business, dealing a major blow to the local economy. Jobs were moved to the Deep South and later offshore.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Location_and_topography">\n        Location and topography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Location and topography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Martinsburg is located at\n       <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion">\n        <a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;params=39_27_33_N_77_58_4_W_type:city">\n         <span class="geo-default">\n          <span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">\n           <span class="latitude">\n            39\xc2\xb027\xe2\x80\xb233\xe2\x80\xb3N\n           </span>\n           <span class="longitude">\n            77\xc2\xb058\xe2\x80\xb24\xe2\x80\xb3W\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         <span class="geo-multi-punct">\n          \xef\xbb\xbf / \xef\xbb\xbf\n         </span>\n         <span class="geo-nondefault">\n          <span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">\n           39.45917\xc2\xb0N 77.96778\xc2\xb0W\n          </span>\n          <span style="display:none">\n           \xef\xbb\xbf /\n           <span class="geo">\n            39.45917; -77.96778\n           </span>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       (39.459207, \xe2\x88\x9277.967814).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR1_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GR1-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As per\n       <a href="/wiki/MapQuest" title="MapQuest">\n        MapQuest\n       </a>\n       , Martinsburg is approximately 92 miles\' (148 km) driving distance northwest of\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_11_in_West_Virginia" title="U.S. Route 11 in West Virginia">\n        U.S. Route 11\n       </a>\n       runs through the center of town, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_81_in_West_Virginia" title="Interstate 81 in West Virginia">\n        Interstate 81\n       </a>\n       passes along the northern side of the town.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       , the city has a total area of 6.67 square miles (17.28\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), of which 6.65 square miles (17.22\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) is land and 0.02 square miles (0.05\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) is water.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gazetteer_files_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gazetteer_files-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">\n        Demographics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Demographics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="toccolours" style="border-spacing: 1px; float: right; clear: right; margin: 0 0 1em 1em; text-align:right">\n       <tr>\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n           [11]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <br/>\n         2014 Estimate\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_Pop_Estimate_12-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-2014_Pop_Estimate-12">\n           [12]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2010_census">\n        2010 census\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2010 census">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">\n        census\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FactFinder_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FactFinder-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       of 2010, there were 17,227 people, 7,293 households, and 4,106 families residing in the city. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">\n        population density\n       </a>\n       was 2,590.5 inhabitants per square mile (1,000.2/km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ). There were 8,408 housing units at an average density of 1,264.4 per square mile (488.2/km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ). The racial makeup of the city was 77.5%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">\n        White\n       </a>\n       , 14.9%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">\n        African American\n       </a>\n       , 0.4%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">\n        Native American\n       </a>\n       , 1.2%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">\n        Asian\n       </a>\n       , 0.1%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(U.S._Census)" title="Race (U.S. Census)">\n        Pacific Islander\n       </a>\n       , 2.3% from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(U.S._Census)" title="Race (U.S. Census)">\n        other races\n       </a>\n       , and 3.7% from two or more races.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">\n        Hispanic\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">\n        Latino\n       </a>\n       of any race were 6.2% of the population.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There were 7,293 households of which 29.6% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 35.3% were\n       <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">\n        married couples\n       </a>\n       living together, 15.0% had a female householder with no husband present, 6.0% had a male householder with no wife present, and 43.7% were non-families. Of all households, 35.4% were made up of individuals and 12.6% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.32 and the average family size was 3.00.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The median age in the city was 37 years. 23.3% of residents were under the age of 18; 8.6% were between the ages of 18 and 24; 28.3% were from 25 to 44; 26.3% were from 45 to 64; and 13.4% were 65 years of age or older. The gender makeup of the city was 48.8% male and 51.2% female.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2000_census">\n        2000 census\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2000 census">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">\n        census\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR2_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GR2-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       of 2000, there were 14,972 people, 6,684 households, and 3,689 families residing in the city. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">\n        population density\n       </a>\n       was 2,977.4 people per square mile (1,149.2/km\xc2\xb2). There were 7,432 housing units at an average density of 1,478.0/sq\xc2\xa0mi (570.5/km\xc2\xb2). The racial makeup of the city was 83.90%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_(U.S._Census)" title="White (U.S. Census)">\n        White\n       </a>\n       , 11.63%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American_(U.S._Census)" title="African American (U.S. Census)">\n        African American\n       </a>\n       , 0.40%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_(U.S._Census)" title="Native American (U.S. Census)">\n        Native American\n       </a>\n       , 0.63%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_(U.S._Census)" title="Asian (U.S. Census)">\n        Asian\n       </a>\n       , 0.02%\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander_(U.S._Census)" title="Pacific Islander (U.S. Census)">\n        Pacific Islander\n       </a>\n       , 1.26% from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">\n        other races\n       </a>\n       , and 2.17% from two or more races.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">\n        Hispanic\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">\n        Latino\n       </a>\n       of any race were 2.91% of the population.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There were 6,684 households out of which 24.9% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 36.7% were\n       <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">\n        married couples\n       </a>\n       living together, 13.7% had a female householder with no husband present, and 44.8% were non-families. 37.6% of all households were made up of individuals and 15.2% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.21 and the average family size was 2.92.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the city, the population was spread out with 23.1% under the age of 18, 9.6% from 18 to 24, 28.7% from 25 to 44, 22.3% from 45 to 64, and 16.4% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 37 years. For every 100 females there were 91.0 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 88.6 males.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The median income for a household in the city was $29,495, and the median income for a family was $36,954. Males had a median income of $29,697 versus $22,212 for females. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">\n        per capita income\n       </a>\n       for the city was $16,314. About 14.7% of families and 20.0% of the population were below the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">\n        poverty line\n       </a>\n       , including 28.8% of those under age 18 and 15.1% of those age 65 or over.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Martinsburg lies in the transition from a\n       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">\n        humid subtropical climate\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        Cfa\n       </i>\n       ) to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">\n        humid continental climate\n       </a>\n       (K\xc3\xb6ppen\n       <i>\n        Dfa\n       </i>\n       ), with four distinct seasons. Winters are cool to cold with a January daily mean temperature of 30.9\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x920.6\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) and an average seasonal snowfall of 26.6 inches (68\xc2\xa0cm), while summers are hot and humid with a July daily mean temperature of 74.7\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (23.7\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) and 27 days of 90\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (32\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C)+ readings annually. Precipitation is moderate, with winter being the driest period and May thru July the wettest. Extreme temperatures range from \xe2\x88\x9218\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9228\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on January 21, 1994 up to 112\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (44\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) on July 11, 1936.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; In February 2015, it was announced that\n       <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">\n        Procter &amp; Gamble\n       </a>\n       plans to build a $500 million facility near the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The city also has numerous federal government employers, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">\n        Internal Revenue Service\n       </a>\n       (IRS),\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Coast_Guard" title="U.S. Coast Guard">\n        U.S. Coast Guard\n       </a>\n       Operations Systems Center,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Coast_Guard" title="U.S. Coast Guard">\n        U.S. Coast Guard\n       </a>\n       National Maritime Center,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Alcohol,_Tobacco,_Firearms,_and_Explosives" title="Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms, and Explosives">\n        Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco, Firearms, and Explosives\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Veterans_Health_Administration" title="Veterans Health Administration">\n        Martinsburg VA Medical Center\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Martinsburg IRS Facility, one of the two Enterprise Computing Centers of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Internal_Revenue_Service" title="Internal Revenue Service">\n        Internal Revenue Service\n       </a>\n       (the other is in\n       <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">\n        Memphis, Tennessee\n       </a>\n       ), processes most of the country\'s electronically filed tax documents from\n       <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">\n        businesses\n       </a>\n       , and about one-third of electronically-filed\n       <a href="/wiki/Tax_return_(United_States)" title="Tax return (United States)">\n        tax returns\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The area is also home to the\n       <a href="/wiki/167th_Airlift_Wing" title="167th Airlift Wing">\n        167th Airlift Wing\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Air_National_Guard" title="West Virginia Air National Guard">\n        West Virginia Air National Guard\n       </a>\n       , based in\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_WV_Regional_Airport" title="Eastern WV Regional Airport">\n        Eastern WV Regional Airport\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Martinsburg had its own automobile company from 1912 to 1922, called Norwalk, which assembled the longest-made known cars to be built in the state of West Virginia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">\n        Sports\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sports">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Future Major League Baseball Hall of Famer\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Hack_Wilson" title="Hack Wilson">\n        Hack Wilson\n       </a>\n       began his storied professional career in his adopted hometown with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Martinsburg_Blue_Sox" title="Martinsburg Blue Sox">\n        Martinsburg Blue Sox\n       </a>\n       , a low-level minor-league baseball team. Wilson would go on to set the yet-to-broken major league record for RBI in a season (191) with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">\n        Chicago Cubs\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in 1930.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After his playing career ended in 1935, Hack went back home to Martinsburg, played some ball with the town\xe2\x80\x99s semipro team and opened a recreation and pool hall in town with a partner. He later moved to Baltimore in 1941 where he later died November 23, 1948. Originally scheduled to be interred in Baltimore, Wilson was buried \xe2\x80\x94 in a donated plot \xe2\x80\x94 in Martinsburg\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       at Rosedale Cemetery.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">\n        Healthcare\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Healthcare">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" medical center\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Berkeley Medical Center (formerly WVUH-East City Hospital and City Hospital)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Veterans Affairs Medical Center\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">\n        Shopping\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Shopping">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Retail centers/areas in Martinsburg include:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Foxcroft_Towne_Center_at_Martinsburg" title="Foxcroft Towne Center at Martinsburg">\n         Foxcroft Towne Center\n        </a>\n        : Walmart and Bon-Ton. There was originally a shopping mall there, but it shut down in late 2016 .Location: Foxcroft Avenue, Interstate 81 Exit 12 &amp; 13.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Commons_Shopping_Center" title="The Commons Shopping Center">\n         The Commons Shopping Center\n        </a>\n        : 400,000 square feet (37,000\xc2\xa0m\n        <sup>\n         2\n        </sup>\n        ) anchored by Target, Dick\'s Sporting Goods, Best Buy, T.J. Maxx, Famous Footwear, Books-A-Million, Bed Bath and Beyond, Michael\'s, Petsmart and Five Below. Opened in 2009. Location: Retail Commons Parkway, Interstate 81 Exit 12.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Old Courthouse Square: 201,350 square feet (18,706\xc2\xa0m\n        <sup>\n         2\n        </sup>\n        ) anchored by Food Lion and Super Shoes. Opened in 1987. Location: Edwin Miller Blvd.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Apple Harvest Drive: K-Mart, Shop \'n Save, Lowes, and Gabe\'s.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        North Queen Street: Weis Markets, Tractor Supply, Big Lots and Aaron\'s.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Other shopping areas in the city are the Berkeley Plaza on Williamsport Pike and Martinsburg Plaza on Winchester Ave.\n        [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transportation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a      West Virginia Route 901\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_transportation">\n        Mass transportation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mass transportation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martinsburg_(Amtrak_station)" title="Martinsburg (Amtrak station)">\n        Martinsburg (Amtrak station)\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       provides service to Martinsburg. The city\'s passenger rail station is located downtown at 229 East Martin Street.\n       <a href="/wiki/MARC_Train" title="MARC Train">\n        MARC\n       </a>\n       , Maryland\'s commuter rail system, operates trains on weekdays on its\n       <a href="/wiki/Brunswick_Line" title="Brunswick Line">\n        Brunswick Line\n       </a>\n       which terminates in Martinsburg. Service is provided to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union_Station_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Union Station (Washington, D.C.)">\n        Union Station\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington, D.C.\n       </a>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Eastern Panhandle Transit Authority operates public bus transit routes in Martinsburg, surrounding Berkeley County, and neighboring\n       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_West_Virginia" title="Jefferson County, West Virginia">\n        Jefferson County, West Virginia\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_WV_Regional_Airport" title="Eastern WV Regional Airport">\n        Eastern WV Regional Airport\n       </a>\n       , south of the city, handles general aviation. The closest airport with commercial air service is\n       <a href="/wiki/Hagerstown_Regional_Airport" title="Hagerstown Regional Airport">\n        Hagerstown Regional Airport\n       </a>\n       , that is about 25 miles (40\xc2\xa0km) driving distance north. The closest international airport is\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">\n        Washington Dulles International Airport\n       </a>\n       near D.C., which is about 60 miles (97\xc2\xa0km) driving distance east.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">\n        Media\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Media">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Print">\n        Print\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Print">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Martinsburg has one daily community newspaper,\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Journal_(West_Virginia_newspaper)" title="The Journal (West Virginia newspaper)">\n         <i>\n          The Journal\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        and also is regionally covered by\n        <a class="external text" href="http://www.heraldmailmedia.com/" rel="nofollow">\n         The Herald-Mail\n        </a>\n        (Hagerstown, MD)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Martinsburg has a bi-monthly magazine,\n        <i>\n         Around the Panhandle\n        </i>\n        magazine.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">\n        Radio\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Radio">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The city is home to\n        <a href="/wiki/WRNR_(AM)" title="WRNR (AM)">\n         WRNR/740 AM\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/WEPM" title="WEPM">\n         WEPM/1340 AM\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/WICL" title="WICL">\n         WICL/95.9 FM\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/WLTF" title="WLTF">\n         WLTF/97.5 FM\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/WVEP" title="WVEP">\n         WVEP/88.9 FM\n        </a>\n        radio stations.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Television">\n        Television\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Television">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Martinsburg is home to W08EE-D Channel 8 (\n        <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Public_Broadcasting" title="West Virginia Public Broadcasting">\n         West Virginia Public Broadcasting\n        </a>\n        ) and (\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWPX" title="WWPX">\n         WWPX\n        </a>\n        60 (\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ION_Television" title="ION Television">\n         ION\n        </a>\n        ), all part of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Hagerstown,_Maryland" title="Hagerstown, Maryland">\n         Hagerstown\n        </a>\n        sub-market that is further grouped under the Nielsen-designated Washington, D.C.-Hagerstown, Md. market, the ninth largest market in the nation.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n         <a href="#cite_note-21">\n          [21]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Martinsburg, WV was the setting of the\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/The_X-Files" title="The X-Files">\n          X-Files\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        episode "\n        <a href="/wiki/Small_Potatoes_(The_X-Files)" title="Small Potatoes (The X-Files)">\n         Small Potatoes\n        </a>\n        " (Season 4, episode 20). However, the filming did not take place in the vicinity.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Martinsburg is the setting for the\n        <a href="/wiki/Reality_television" title="Reality television">\n         reality television\n        </a>\n        series\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Gypsy_Sisters" title="Gypsy Sisters">\n          Gypsy Sisters\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        on\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/TLC_(TV_network)" title="TLC (TV network)">\n          TLC\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Martinsburg is the town used for making the movie,\n        <a href="/wiki/Sweet_Dreams_(1985_film)" title="Sweet Dreams (1985 film)">\n         <i>\n          Sweet Dreams\n         </i>\n        </a>\n        , starring\n        <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Lange" title="Jessica Lange">\n         Jessica Lange\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a href="/wiki/Ed_Harris" title="Ed Harris">\n         Ed Harris\n        </a>\n        , portraying the life of First Lady of Country Music,\n        <a href="/wiki/Patsy_Cline" title="Patsy Cline">\n         Pasty Cline\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">\n        Notable people\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Martinsburg,_West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notable people">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Jacob_M._Appel" title="Jacob M.
